I.      INTRODUCTION
This report summarizes the current traffic and parking conditions in the Cherry Creek business
district, shopping district and residential neighborhood. This report provides an update to a
parking inventory and occupancy evaluation that was conducted in the summer and fall of 2010,
the summary report for which was issued in February 2011 (February 2011 Report). There are
two notable changes between the two inventory efforts:

     1. Parking meters (Denver Smart Meters) have replaced the kiosks in the Cherry Creek
        North Commercial Area since the previous evaluation was conducted. Under the kiosk
        system vehicles generally parked slightly closer together during peak demand periods
        than the current meter spacing allows, resulting in a loss of capacity in the metered area
        of one to two spaces per block on east-west blocks and two to five spaces on north-
        south blocks.

     2. In addition to parking conditions, this report includes information on current traffic
        volumes and travel speeds within the study area, and also includes an inventory of
        bicycle parking throughout the study area.

Figure 1 shows the extent of the parking study area as well as the locations where traffic and
speed data was collected.

All data was collected in January 2013. Daily traffic counts and speed data were recorded
Thursday, January 17th, 2013 through Saturday, January 19th, 2013, intersection turning
movement traffic counts were recorded on Thursday, January 17th, 2013, and all parking data
was recorded on Friday, January 18th, 2013. There were clear skies and daytime temperatures
in the 40s and 50s on each of the three data collection days, so weather conditions did not
impact the data collection effort or results.

The following parking data was recorded in each sub area:

        Cherry Creek North Commercial Area
           o Typical parking space lengths on blocks with unmarked spaces
           o Current parking space occupancy during the mid-day and evening peak periods
           o Typical length of stay trends for the various types of parking time restrictions in
               the area

        Cherry Creek North Residential Area
           o Overall parking utilization and parking utilization in both the two-hour parking
               spaces and Residential Parking Permit (RPP)-designated spaces
           o Utilization of the RPP-designated spaces by vehicles with a valid RPP permit

II.    EXISTING TRAFFIC COUNTS AND TRAVEL SPEED DATA
A.     Existing Traffic Counts

Daily traffic volumes and vehicle turning movements were recorded throughout the Cherry
Creek study area in January 2013. A total of 35 daily traffic counts and 24 intersection turning
movement counts were collected. The turning movement data was collected in 15-minute
increments for two hours during the morning peak traffic period, and again for two hours during
the afternoon peak period, and then the highest one hour period within each two-hour window
was reported. Historical hourly traffic counts indicated that in the Cherry Creek area the two
hour morning peak period begins at 7 AM and ends around 9 AM, while the afternoon peak
period begins at 4 PM and ends around 6 PM. Figure 2 shows the current weekday traffic
volumes, Figure 3 shows the current Saturday traffic volumes, and Figure 4 shows the morning
and afternoon peak hour vehicle turning movements and pedestrian crossing volumes. The raw
peak hour traffic data is included in Appendix A.

As shown on Figure 2, weekday traffic volumes along 1st Avenue/Cherry Creek Drive North
range from 38,000 to 40,000 vehicles per day (vpd) east and west of the Cherry Creek North
Commercial Area, and increase to approximately 50,000 vpd between University and Steele
through the heart of the commercial area. Within the Cherry Creek North street system, daily
traffic volumes generally range from 4,000 to 7,000 vpd between 1st Avenue and 3rd Avenue (in
the core of the commercial area), and from 1,200 to 2,400 vpd north of 3rd Avenue (land uses
transition from commercial to residential between 3rd and 4th Avenue and are residential north of
4th Avenue).

As shown on Figure 3, Saturday volumes on 1st Avenue/Cherry Creek Drive North average 31-
33,000 vpd east and west of the Cherry Creek North Commercial Area and 42-43,000 vpd
through the heart of the commercial area, while traffic on the street system within Cherry Creek
North averages 2,500 to 6,000 vpd in the commercial area and 1,000 to 2,000 vpd in the
residential area. In general, weekend traffic volumes throughout Cherry Creek North are around
20 percent lower than during the week.

B.     Existing Travel Speeds

In addition to traffic volume data, vehicle travel speed data was also recorded at several
locations throughout the study area. In practice, the 85th percentile speed (the speed at which
85 percent of all drivers travel at or below) is considered the upper limit of a reasonable travel
speed for a roadway and therefore is typically used to set speed limits on roadways. The 85th
percentile travel speeds collected for roadways in the Cherry Creek area are shown on Figure
5. The posted speed limit on 1st Avenue at the Gilpin data collection location is 30 mph, while
the posted speed at all other data collection locations is 25 mph. As the figure indicates, most
of the 85th percentile travel speeds on the were within 5 mph of the 25 mph posted speed, and
only four locations (1st Avenue east of Gilpin (38 mph), Gilpin north of 1st (29 mph), Milwaukee
north of 3rd (27 mph) and St. Paul north of 3rd (30 mph)) reported 85th percentile travel speeds
that exceeded the posted speed.

Cherry Creek Area                                      Parking and Traffic Conditions Inventory


II. CHERRY CREEK NORTH COMMERCIAL AREA PARKING
CONDITIONS
A.     Existing Signed Parking Restrictions

The existing signed parking restrictions in the Cherry Creek North Commercial Area are shown
on Figure 6. The figure shows the numbering convention developed for each of the blocks
within the sub area, as well as the locations of no parking zones scattered throughout the area.
As indicated, the majority of the Cherry Creek North Commercial Area is comprised of metered
parking (up to 3-hours) with both Residential Parking Permit (RPP) and 2-hour parking zones
along the north edge (4th Avenue).

In general, the duration of the metered time restrictions within the commercial area run from 8
AM to 7 PM. This is also true for the signed 2-hour parking and the RPP-designated block
faces.

B.     Parking Data Collection Methodology

Parking data was collected in the Cherry Creek North Commercial Area on Friday, January 18,
2013. As with the previous Cherry Creek parking study, Friday conditions were selected
because historical observations in the area indicated that the combined demand created by
office, retail, restaurant and residential activities peaks on that day.

The previous study collected parking data each hour from 8 AM to 9 PM, and indicated that the
parking demand peaked during the early afternoon, and then again in the evening. In light of
this, parking occupancy data was collected from 1 PM to 2 PM and 7 PM to 8 PM to capture
those peak conditions. During each period, the number of cars parked was recorded for each
block face within the study area. In addition to this parking occupancy data, parking duration
data was collected between 1 PM and 9 PM for a smaller four block sub area of the Cherry
Creek North Commercial Area, bounded by Clayton Street on the west, 3rd Street on the north,
Saint Paul Street on the east and 2nd Street on the south. This effort included collecting partial
license plate numbers of all parked vehicles every hour during study period to determine how
long each vehicle occupied its on-street space. All of the data were then analyzed to determine
overall parking patterns in the area. For more information on the results of the duration study,
see Table 2 on page 15.

C.     Typical Curb Space Usage by Parked Vehicles

The data on length of curb space used per parked vehicle collected for the February 2011
Report (i.e., prior to replacing the kiosks with meters) was re-used in this inventory to determine
the available number of on-street parking spaces on the signed block faces in the Cherry Creek
North Commercial Area. Table 1 shows the block locations, number of vehicles parked, total
curb space occupied and average parking space length per vehicle for all instances where a
block was fully occupied during the data collection effort for the February 2011 Report. As the
table indicates, a vehicle parked within the Cherry Creek North Commercial Area typically
occupies around 20 feet of curb space.

D.     Cherry Creek North Commercial Area Parking Supply

The total number of on-street parking spaces available within the Cherry Creek North
Commercial Area was calculated for each block based on either the number of parking meters
or the length of the block face and the 20 feet per parking space assumption from above. Based
on these parameters, there are approximately 850 on-street parking spaces in the portion of the
Cherry Creek North Commercial Area inventoried for this report.

E.     Cherry Creek North Commercial Area Parking Occupancy

The results of the Cherry Creek North Commercial Area parking occupancy study are presented
on Figures 7 and 8. Each block face has been color-coded to correspond with the level of
occupancy observed during the data collection period. The on-street parking occupancy from 1
PM to 2 PM (daytime peak) is shown on Figure 7 while the parking occupancy information for 7
PM to 8 PM (evening peak) is shown on Figure 8. Of note, the evening peak counts were
conducted after the time restrictions for the Cherry Creek North metered parking area had
ended, when vehicles were not limited to the three-hour restriction in the metered area or the
two-hour restriction on the non-metered blocks. The figures show the total number of on-street
spaces, the number of occupied spaces, and the number of open spaces on each block.

Cherry Creek Area                                       Parking and Traffic Conditions Inventory


As both of these figures show, a significant number of block faces experience peak occupancies
in excess of 70 percent in both the day and the evening--the level at which it is more likely for a
driver to see on-street parking as increasingly challenging because they typically cannot find a
space in front of or adjacent to their destination. Specifically, 46 of the 73 block faces during the
day and 53 of 73 in the evening have occupancy levels greater than 70 percent, indicating that
on-street parking is well-utilized throughout the area at all times. Overall, on-street parking is
between 70 and 75 percent occupied during both peak periods. In particular, the block faces
along or immediately adjacent to 2nd Avenue in the south and southwestern portion of the study
area (centered around the 2nd and Clayton intersection) are in high demand; they experience
occupancies in excess of 70 percent, and often in excess of 85 percent (essentially full) during
both periods. In the evening, when demand is the highest in the commercial area, the 70+ and
85+ percent full blocks extend further east and west from the 2nd and Clayton node than they do
during the day, but the additional demand does not appear to extend further north--north of 3rd
Avenue, the block faces generally have occupancies less than 70 percent during the evening,
which is similar to their daytime occupancies.

It should be noted that there are two north-south block faces north of 3rd Avenue with
occupancies greater than 70 percent (the east side of Fillmore and the east side of St. Paul)
during the day, but it should be also be noted that throughout the day the west sides of those
streets are reserved for those vehicles with RPP stickers or hanging tags, which shifts any non-
RPP vehicles to the east side and somewhat skews the distribution there. This finding is similar
to that reported in the February 2011 Report.

Finally, the occupancy percentage in the paid on-street parking spaces is higher in 2013 than it
was in 2010. There are two possible contributing factors for this; first, the retail vacancy rates in
Cherry Creek North are lower now than they were three years ago, so the additional occupied
retail space is attracting additional retail customers. Second, the metered block parking
capacities are lower now than they were with kiosks in place; under the kiosk system vehicles
generally parked slightly closer together during peak demand periods than the current meter
spacing allows, resulting in a loss of capacity in the metered area of one to two spaces per
block on east-west blocks and two to five spaces on north-south blocks.

Appendix B includes tables with on-street parking data for the Cherry Creek North Commercial
Area.

F.     Compliance with On-Street Time Restrictions and Parking Turnover

As noted previously, a parking duration evaluation was completed for a four block sub area of
the Cherry Creek North Commercial Area. All of the block faces within this sub area provide
metered parking. The metered parking is in effect between 8 AM and 7 PM and allows for a
vehicle to park for up to three hours at a time. The vast majority of the vehicles parked within
these time limited zones complied with the posted restrictions, with only 22 of the 709 observed
vehicles parking for longer than three hours.

Table 2 compares the parking duration data from this study with the duration data collected in
the parking kiosk area from the February 2011 Report. Both sets of data indicate an average
length of stay of around an hour and a half. The most recent counts indicated a five percent
increase in vehicles parking for more than two hours when compared to the previous study.
Overall, however, nine out of 10 vehicles still park for less than two hours.

G.      Bicycle Parking Inventory

Finally, as part of this reevaluation, the location and capacity of bike racks located throughout
the Cherry Creek North area were recorded. The results of the field survey can be seen on
Figure 9. As can be seen on this figure, there are a total of 63 bike racks in the area with an
estimated capacity of approximately 337 bikes. In addition, there are two Denver B-Cycle racks
that can accommodate a total of 26 B-Cycle bikes.

III. CHERRY CREEK NORTH RESIDENTIAL AREA PARKING
CONDITIONS
A.     Parking Data Collection Methodology

As with the Cherry Creek North Commercial Area, parking data was collected in the Cherry
Creek North Residential Area on Friday January 18, 2013. The study area is bounded by 6th
Avenue to the north, Steele Street to the east, 4th Avenue to the south and University to the
west. Parking data was collected between 1 PM and 2 PM and again after 8 PM to correspond
with the mid-day and evening peak demand periods in the residential area. During each time
period, in addition to collecting vehicle occupancy counts for each block face, the number of
vehicles with a RPP permit was also noted to assess the level of compliance on block faces that
are reserved for RPP permit holders.

B.     Signed Parking Restrictions

The existing signed parking restrictions in the Cherry Creek North Residential Area are
presented on Figure 10. The figure shows the numbering convention developed for each of the
blocks within the sub area, as well as the locations of no parking zones scattered throughout the
area. As Figure 10 indicates, the study area generally has a mix of unrestricted, 1-hour and 2-
hour parking along 6th Avenue (with the time limited-spaces active between 8 AM and 6 PM).
Within the residential neighborhood, parking is generally comprised of 2-hour parking zones on
the east and north faces of each block and RPP zones on the west and south faces. In doing
so, one side of any given street is available for 2-hour parking by anyone, while the other side of
the street is reserved for only those vehicles that have valid RPP stickers or hanging tags for the
area. The RPP-designated block faces are in effect between 8 AM and 7 PM, the same duration
period as the timed restrictions in the Cherry Creek North Commercial Area.

C.     Cherry Creek North Residential Area Parking Supply

The total number of on-street parking spaces available within the Cherry Creek North
Residential Area was calculated for each block based on the 20 feet per vehicle length
observed in the Cherry Creek North Commercial Area. Based on these parameters, there are
approximately 815 on-street spaces in the portion of the residential area reevaluated for this
study.

D.     Cherry Creek North Residential Area Parking Occupancy

The results of the Cherry Creek North Residential Area occupancy counts and permit
verification are presented on Figures 11 and 12. As with the Cherry Creek North Commercial
Area, each block face has been color coded to correspond with the occupancy observed during
the data collection period. The on-street parking occupancy from 1 PM to 2 PM (daytime peak
period) is presented on Figure 11 while the parking occupancy information after 8 PM (evening
peak period) is presented on Figure 12. It should be noted that the evening peak period is after
the time restrictions for the parking permit program in the area have ended, so anyone can park
on any block face for as long as needed at that time. The figures show the number of on-street
spaces available, the number of spaces occupied and the number of parked vehicles that had a
valid RPP sticker or hanging tag visible.

Cherry Creek Area                                     Parking and Traffic Conditions Inventory


As both of the occupancy figures show, there is ample parking supply in the Cherry Creek North
Residential Area; of the 50 block faces studied, only eight during the day and seven in the
evening had occupancies greater than 50 percent. Furthermore, only two blocks faces had
occupancies greater than 70 percent; St. Paul Street between 6th and 5th Avenues (77 percent
during the day) and 6th Avenue between Milwaukee and St. Paul (86 percent in the evening).
Both of those block faces are near several restaurants on 6th Avenue with limited on-site
parking, and neither are designated for RPP-only parking. It is therefore likely that both are
attracting the spill-over demand from those establishments.

Of the 29 RPP-designated block faces in the residential area, only one (the west side of St. Paul
Street between 4th and 5th Avenues, where all 12 vehicles parked on that block had RPP
permits) had an occupancy greater than 50 percent during the day, when the RPP-only
designation was active. At the same time, only seven of the 29 block faces within that area that
don't have RPP designations had occupancies greater than 50 percent during the day (the
aforementioned St. Paul between 5th and 6th, plus Clayton between 4th and 5th, Clayton between
5th and 6th, Detroit between 4th and 5th, 5th between Detroit and Fillmore, 6th between Josephine
and Columbine, and 6th between Detroit and Fillmore). These observations suggest that the
RPP program is meeting the intent of deterring long-term, non-resident parking during the day in
the residential area, both on RPP-designated blocks and on unrestricted blocks.

Finally, the vast majority of vehicles parked on RPP-only designated block faces were observed
to have a visible RPP sticker or hanging tag (96 percent during the daytime observation when
the RPP-only designation was active, and 91 percent during the evening observation when the
RPP-only designation had ended). Furthermore, the overall utilization for those spaces ranged
from 15 percent during the day, when the RPP-only designation was active, to 19-24 percent in
the evening when the RPP-only designation had ended. These low occupancy rates suggest
that the number of parking spaces reserved for those vehicles with residential parking permits is
significantly greater than the actual demand for those spaces. Appendix C includes tables with
on-street parking data for the Cherry Creek North Residential Area.




                                                                                         Page 22
Cherry Creek Area                                       Parking and Traffic Conditions Inventory


IV.      STUDY CONCLUSIONS AND RECOMMENDATIONS
This report summarizes the current traffic and parking conditions in the Cherry Creek North
area, and represents an update to a similar report completed in February, 2011. This analysis
focuses on the Cherry Creek North Commercial Area and Cherry Creek North Residential Area,
and, in addition to parking data, also provides daily and peak hour traffic count data and bicycle
parking information.

Parking inventory and utilization data collected on Friday January 18, 2013, as well as traffic
volume and speed data collected January 17 through January 19, 2013 were used in this
analysis. The data indicated the following:

Traffic Volume and Speed Data

         Weekday traffic volumes typically range from 4,000 to 7,000 vpd in the commercial area
         between 1st Avenue and 3rd Avenue.
         Weekday traffic volumes in the residential area north of 3rd Avenue typically range from
         1,200 to 2,400 vpd, with only one location above 2,000 vpd.
         Traffic volumes in the area are around 20 percent lower on the weekend than during the
         week.
         The posted speed limit 1st Avenue/Cherry Creek North Drive is 30 mph, and the 85th
         percentile travel speed east of Gilpin is eight mph higher than that (38 mph).
         The posted speed limit on the other local roadways where data was collected is 25 mph.
         All of the recorded 85th percentile travel speeds were within 5 mph of this posted speed,
         and only three locations (Gilpin north of 1st, Milwaukee north of 3rd and St. Paul north of
         3rd) exceeded the posted speed.

Cherry Creek North Commercial Area Parking Conditions

         A significant number of block faces in the Cherry Creek North Commercial Area
         experience a peak hour occupancy in excess of 70 percent in both the day and the
         evening--the level at which drivers begin to see on-street parking as somewhat
         problematic because they typically cannot find a space in front of or adjacent to their
         destination. 46 of the 73 block faces during the day and 53 of 73 in the evening have
         occupancy levels greater than 70 percent, indicating that on-street parking is well utilized
         throughout the area at all times.
         The utilization data indicates that several blocks within the commercial area have
         parking demands that extend past 8 PM.
         The highest occupied block faces are generally located around 2nd Avenue/Clayton
         Street in the south and southwestern portion of the study area, and parking demand to
         the east and west is higher in the evening than in the afternoon.
         Around 60 percent of the patrons parking in the metered spaces stay for one hour or
         less, and 90 percent park for less than 2 hours. The average length of stay of all
         metered parking users is about an hour and a half.




                                                                                             Page 23
Cherry Creek Area                                    Parking and Traffic Conditions Inventory


Cherry Creek North Residential Area Parking Conditions

       In general, parking supply is ample in the Cherry Creek North Residential Area, of the 58
       block faces studied in that area, 50 during the day and 51 in the evening were less than
       50 percent occupied. Of those block faces with more than 50 percent occupancy, only
       two (one during the day and one in the evening) had occupancies greater than 70
       percent. When the aggregate occupancy levels exceed 70 percent, it is more likely for a
       driver to perceive on-street parking as increasingly challenging because they typically
       cannot find a space in front of or adjacent to their destination.
       The current Residential Parking Permit and 2-hour parking designations in the Cherry
       Creek North Residential Area are deterring spill over from the Cherry Creek North
       Commercial Area; only three of the block faces that border the commercial sub area had
       occupancies greater than 50 percent in either the day or the evening.
       The overall utilization for those spaces in the residential area that are reserved for RPP
       holders ranged from 15 percent occupied during the day when the RPP-only designation
       was active to 19-24 percent occupied in the evening when the RPP-only designation had
       ended. This would appear to indicate that the number of parking spaces reserved for
       residential parking permit holders is significantly greater than the actual demand for
       those spaces.
